  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f3eab662-3ed1-482c-b2c7-3b1d694d4192'
      });

<div id="review_256020553" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/256020553" />
    <a title="Alvi Harahap" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5425105-alvi-harahap"><img alt="Alvi Harahap" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1323055769p2/5425105.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/256020553?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alvi Harahap" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alvi Harahap" href="/user/show/5425105-alvi-harahap">Alvi Harahap</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789792261585" href="/book/show/9255345-the-crossing-of-ingo">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer256020553" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8077548761051534404">Helen Dunmore, a British author, well known for her books for children, has come out with yet another fantasy series called the Ingo series. Initially a trilogy, it soon went onto become a series with a total of 4 books. Ingo is the 1st book of the series. A fan of Harry Potter, I picked this book just by glancing at its cover…it featured a mermaid. :)<br/><br/>The story is about the adventures of Connor and Sapphire, who loose their father to the world of Ingo. He is believed to have drowned but Connor a</span>
  <span id="freeText8077548761051534404" style="display:none">Helen Dunmore, a British author, well known for her books for children, has come out with yet another fantasy series called the Ingo series. Initially a trilogy, it soon went onto become a series with a total of 4 books. Ingo is the 1st book of the series. A fan of Harry Potter, I picked this book just by glancing at its cover…it featured a mermaid. :)<br /><br />The story is about the adventures of Connor and Sapphire, who loose their father to the world of Ingo. He is believed to have drowned but Connor and Sapphire refuse to believe that their father is dead. As they and their mother struggle to get through the life without their father, Connor discovers the world of Ingo through Elvira, a mermaid who befriends Connor, and Sapphire soon follows Connor into Ingo with the help of her merfriend Faro. Sapphire becomes obsessed with the sea and Ingo owing to her strong mixed human-merpeople heritage. Unlike Connor who has more of the Air or Earth spirit in him, Sapphire’s Water/Ingo spirit dominates her thought process. As they delve deeper into this new world, they discover the whereabouts of their father, who turns into a merman and has a whole new mer-family. The story then moves to describe the different aspects of the ocean that Sapphire and Connor discover including their mer powers, and concludes with the family moving from Cornwall to a new location.<br /><br />This fantasy series is quite enjoyable to read if you are an avid fan of merpeople and legends as such. One will appreciate the adaptable and more matured Connor when compared to the stubborn and hard headed Sapphire, who is quite intent on escaping the human world and her problems. On the whole, this is a good to read book. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8077548761051534404" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2713510342" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2713510342" />
    <a title="Div" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18532397-div"><img alt="Div" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526850072p2/18532397.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2713510342?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Div" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Div" href="/user/show/18532397-div">Div</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2713510342&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2713510342" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9124914970414092010">I enjoyed this one the most out of all the novels in the series. There was excitement and adventure like no other. So much happened in this one.<br/><br/>The kids are definitely growing up here. The Call has magically cleared the path for Sapphire and Conor to make The Crossing of Ingo which is pivotal to begin the process of healing the rift between Air and Ingo. Their mixed blood and the theme of not belonging by belonging to two seemingly separate worlds is a beautiful one as it transcends this literal</span>
  <span id="freeText9124914970414092010" style="display:none">I enjoyed this one the most out of all the novels in the series. There was excitement and adventure like no other. So much happened in this one.<br /><br />The kids are definitely growing up here. The Call has magically cleared the path for Sapphire and Conor to make The Crossing of Ingo which is pivotal to begin the process of healing the rift between Air and Ingo. Their mixed blood and the theme of not belonging by belonging to two seemingly separate worlds is a beautiful one as it transcends this literal difference laid out and echoes the many differences in our own world and the struggle of anyone who is mixed and finds himself/herself not wholly fitting into one rigid mould set by our society.<br /><br />Elvira finally gets development and her relationship with the other more prominent characters, Sapphire, Conor and Faro are developed. She is finally fleshed out and I feel like I finally get a sense of who she is. The dynamics of this group of four also grows and changes. I thought that this was quite interesting.<br /><br />Magic. I always love more magic. That dream/real/it's all happening inside of your head but it doesn't mean it isn't real sequence was great! Mom's character is developed. How wonderful! We finally get some stuff on her. That strange Atka or ghost or whatever has me intrigued and I hope I see her again. <br /><br />Finally, the grand showdown was not a disappointment like the fearsome Kraken of The Deep. Way to go Dad! And OMG Conor! It was exciting! Also, the feelings of Conor showed that the victory was not celebrated as it usually is in many battles. What he did, despite the justification, is hard and that should never be forgotten. I thought that this was handled quite well.<br /><br />So, why not 5 stars!? It's because I'm difficult to please. I really liked this book. There is no doubt. But it did not blow my mind entirely. I didn't totally fan girl, obsess over it and utterly lose myself in it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9124914970414092010" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_84877771" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/84877771" />
    <a title="Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1762033-elizabeth"><img alt="Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491327487p2/1762033.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/84877771?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth" href="/user/show/1762033-elizabeth">Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1762033-elizabeth?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1762033-elizabeth?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1762033-elizabeth?shelf=mermaids-and-sea-creatures">mermaids-and-sea-creatures</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer84877771&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer84877771" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13666211256026274728">Sapphire, Conor, Faro, and Elvira make the crossing of Ingo. Conor and Elvira break up, Sapphire is christened "friend of Ingo", Faro comes to terms with his human blood, Saldowr is Dumbledore, Ervys dies, Helen Dunmore adds in "save the whales" subtext wherever she can. Ta daaa. So ends the Ingo series.<br/><br/>It was a decent book and a decent series. I think the issue is that I may be too old for it now. I read the first one three and a half years before this one. I need to stop doing that with series</span>
  <span id="freeText13666211256026274728" style="display:none">Sapphire, Conor, Faro, and Elvira make the crossing of Ingo. Conor and Elvira break up, Sapphire is christened "friend of Ingo", Faro comes to terms with his human blood, Saldowr is Dumbledore, Ervys dies, Helen Dunmore adds in "save the whales" subtext wherever she can. Ta daaa. So ends the Ingo series.<br /><br />It was a decent book and a decent series. I think the issue is that I may be too old for it now. I read the first one three and a half years before this one. I need to stop doing that with series. I think I was also kind of waiting for the moment for somebody to shout, DAD. WHY DID YOU LEAVE US. WHY DID YOU BECOME MER. <i>HOW</i> DID YOU BECOME MER? WHERE DID OUR MER BLOOD COME FROM. WE ARE ANGRY AT YOU. But none of that really... happened. Nobody ever said anything. Everyone's anger was all very suppressed and I was quite enraged and feel like I never received a proper apology from the father! <br /><br />And I still don't really understand what was so great about Ingo. There was something so foreboding about it underneath all the glittery fish and pretty colours and warm water. Maybe because I'm really not a big fan of the water myself. I'd much rather be up in the air with trees and fire and land and rainbows and cats and dry hair. But that's just me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13666211256026274728" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8576886230895229722">A nice conclusion to the series. I really love the premise of the Crossing of Ingo. I enjoyed all of the voyage arc. I was a bit disappointed in the ending, some actions in particular felt very out of character <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ I mean, Connor killing Ervys... really? <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> In general, I got a bit frustrated with the inconsistencies that littered the series. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[In book 2 Faro loses contiousness trying to join Sapphire in the deep, and yet in book 3 he can go without any issue</span></span>
  <span id="freeText8576886230895229722" style="display:none">A nice conclusion to the series. I really love the premise of the Crossing of Ingo. I enjoyed all of the voyage arc. I was a bit disappointed in the ending, some actions in particular felt very out of character <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I mean, Connor killing Ervys... really? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> In general, I got a bit frustrated with the inconsistencies that littered the series. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[In book 2 Faro loses contiousness trying to join Sapphire in the deep, and yet in book 3 he can go without any issues. Connor is supposed to have weaker Mer blood than Sapphire and yet that is very quickly resolved without much of an explanation. Sometimes entering/exiting Ingo hurts the characters and inexplicably, this fluctuates. You'd think it'd be a process of getting used to it/giving into their Mer/Earth inheritance, but it isn't consistent in that way. I'm rambling and nitpicking, but there are lots of little details that just don't quite add up.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> As in the previous books, it always seems like things happen very easily and conveniently. But overall Dunmore does a good job of bringing things to a conclusion and giving meaning to the events in the previous books. I just wish there would have been (even just a tiny bit) more romance between the main characters.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9818550617974685876">The last book in the series. When the call is sounded, all the young of Ingo that hear it go on the 'Crossing' - an epic swim around the oceans of the world. Sapphy and Conner, although half human and living in Air, are called too. But Ervys and his followers don't want any half-bloods polluting the tradition. They want Ingo to be pure and to fight back against the encroachments of humans, while Saldowr believes that it is the half-bloods that will bring healing to both Ingo and Air. Connor, Sap</span>
  <span id="freeText9818550617974685876" style="display:none">The last book in the series. When the call is sounded, all the young of Ingo that hear it go on the 'Crossing' - an epic swim around the oceans of the world. Sapphy and Conner, although half human and living in Air, are called too. But Ervys and his followers don't want any half-bloods polluting the tradition. They want Ingo to be pure and to fight back against the encroachments of humans, while Saldowr believes that it is the half-bloods that will bring healing to both Ingo and Air. Connor, Sapphy, Elvira and Faro set off together, deciding to head North to avoid the sharks that Ervys has sent to stop them. They face killer whales, hungry polar bears and Northern spirits, but have to work together to succeed.<br /><br />This is a much darker story than the rest. The starving animals of the North was a point belaboured so much that it spoilt the enjoyment of the story for me. I did like the idea of the crossing though and, although the ending is very sad, it was a good one. All in all, I have enjoyed reading this series, a complete change from the authors adult books. </span>

<div id="review_2909697272" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2909697272" />
    <a title="Eskana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4822415-eskana"><img alt="Eskana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339462379p2/4822415.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2909697272?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eskana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eskana" href="/user/show/4822415-eskana">Eskana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2909697272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2157278116486540105"><b>Plot Synopsis:</b> Conner and Sapphire are again called by Ingo, this time to make the journey that all young Mer must make: the Crossing of Ingo. Alone, they must travel to the bottom of the world and back to prove they are true Mer. This time though, Ervys has gathered followers who are against anyone with ANY human blood in Ingo, and will do anything to stop them. On the journey, the siblings and their friends will discover their own identities and where their future lies.<br/><br/><b>Review:</b> This was a good </span>
  <span id="freeText2157278116486540105" style="display:none"><b>Plot Synopsis:</b> Conner and Sapphire are again called by Ingo, this time to make the journey that all young Mer must make: the Crossing of Ingo. Alone, they must travel to the bottom of the world and back to prove they are true Mer. This time though, Ervys has gathered followers who are against anyone with ANY human blood in Ingo, and will do anything to stop them. On the journey, the siblings and their friends will discover their own identities and where their future lies.<br /><br /><b>Review:</b> This was a good end to the Ingo series. Like all the other Ingo books, it really sucked me into the world. In the previous books, I always felt like I'd been suck into Ingo too, and would lose track of time between the two worlds. When I stopped reading, I'd feel like I'd been away a long time, like Ingo and my world really were on different time schedules. <br />This one is like that, but a little less so, since the majority of the book takes place in Ingo. It begins actually without Sappy or Conner, but with the Call being made to summon the young Mer. They hear it, realize the must follow it, and make their plans to be away for a while (surprisingly easy for two unsupervised children.) Also, the threat of Ervys is barely there, to be honest. He tries a few things at first, but our group of heroes quickly realizes that he'll be threatening them every step of the way, so they decide to get to the bottom of the world by going over the North Pole, thereby avoiding all problems. <br />The Pole part is pretty cool, and the overall journey was interesting although pretty calm since they'd avoided the bad guys. They did show up at the end of course, but the climax was pretty quick. At the end, though, I really feel that the characters have grown and matured since they'd first entered Ingo and really started to become little adults. It was a good ending.<br /><br />Consequently, I don't think the author could go any farther with these characters; they've really done it all. (Personally, I'm also a little tired of Faro and his ocean-sized ego that never changes, and Elvira, who's just kinda there and doesn't get along with anyone.) I'd like to see a bit of a reversal, if anything, with the Mer characters being able to come on land, but I don't see how that could happen.<br /><br /><b>All in all,</b> a good finish to the series, although probably not the strongest or most exciting book in it. Good reads.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="2157278116486540105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3092256825" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3092256825" />
    <a title="Celina M" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73254927-celina-m"><img alt="Celina M" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3092256825?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celina M" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celina M" href="/user/show/73254927-celina-m">Celina M</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3092256825" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17139979757617058267">4.25 stars.<br/><br/>A good ending to the series, playing to the series’ strengths by exploring more of Ingo. While the ‘villain’/conflict wasn’t really an effective ‘bad guy’, it was a small enough part of the story that it didn’t matter. The ending and character’s conclusions I felt were really well done. I like that Elvira and Connor didn’t get together, acknowledging they are teenagers, and you don’t meet your soulmate at 14. I also liked that Sapphire and Faro’s stories ended with just “I’m 14 and I </span>
  <span id="freeText17139979757617058267" style="display:none">4.25 stars.<br /><br />A good ending to the series, playing to the series’ strengths by exploring more of Ingo. While the ‘villain’/conflict wasn’t really an effective ‘bad guy’, it was a small enough part of the story that it didn’t matter. The ending and character’s conclusions I felt were really well done. I like that Elvira and Connor didn’t get together, acknowledging they are teenagers, and you don’t meet your soulmate at 14. I also liked that Sapphire and Faro’s stories ended with just “I’m 14 and I don’t have to choose my future now,” which I think is a good ending for teenagers. Although I still wish there was a scene where Faro would visit the land, the ending felt good and hopeful, and was a satisfying conclusion for the series.</span>

<div id="review_3352613022" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3352613022" />
    <a title="Marsha Dermott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75999058-marsha-dermott"><img alt="Marsha Dermott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516639355p2/75999058.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3352613022?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marsha Dermott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marsha Dermott" href="/user/show/75999058-marsha-dermott">Marsha Dermott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3352613022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1685143013419698879">This is the fourth and final book in the Ingo series. With each book, Dunmore plunges the reader further into the world of Ingo beneath the sea and the politics of the Mer people. I became spellbound over the four books,reading them in quick succession, giving the last two books five star ratings for sheer sustainability of thought-provoking adventure that is so very relevant for it's older children/teen readers.<br/>I am now suffering from a massive book hangover. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Sen Matsuri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/70234507-sen-matsuri"><img alt="Sen Matsuri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515690135p2/70234507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2291160955?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sen Matsuri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sen Matsuri" href="/user/show/70234507-sen-matsuri">Sen Matsuri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2291160955" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6783746852961594149">The Crossing of Ingo is the book of changes and choices. The changes of Ingo, the choices of the Mer, the maturity of our lovely protagonists... and the changes of the heart. As always, Helen Dunmore has created a mystery yet beautiful Ingo, where I can easily follow the fantastic journey to the bottom of the world with Conor, Sapphire, Faro and Elvira… The fourth book has so many developments in the plot that I find myself both eager and anxious to read the final book of the Ingo series. <br/>What m</span>
  <span id="freeText6783746852961594149" style="display:none">The Crossing of Ingo is the book of changes and choices. The changes of Ingo, the choices of the Mer, the maturity of our lovely protagonists... and the changes of the heart. As always, Helen Dunmore has created a mystery yet beautiful Ingo, where I can easily follow the fantastic journey to the bottom of the world with Conor, Sapphire, Faro and Elvira… The fourth book has so many developments in the plot that I find myself both eager and anxious to read the final book of the Ingo series. <br />What makes this book stand out from its three previous ones is that Dunmore has expressed sorrow and fury – more exquisitely, I perceive – of the destructions human has done to the marine ecosystems, which are cleverly added to inherent details of fantasies and adventures of the series.<br />Thank you Helen Dunmore for bringing the wonderful world of Ingo to me.</span>

<div id="review_805699255" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/805699255" />
    <a title="Maggie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9968964-maggie"><img alt="Maggie" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/805699255?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie" href="/user/show/9968964-maggie">Maggie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer805699255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14806971462115380915">Okay, I have fallen hopelessly in love with Ingo since sixth grade. For some obnoxious reason, The Crossing of Ingo wasn't available in American libraries, so I had to buy it--which totally wasn't a problem because no matter how old I will get these books will always have a special place in my heart. :)<br/>GOOD STUFF!:<br/>To be brief, I was not disappointed!! I was SO HAPPY to see that Connor got over Elvira. I don't have any specific problem with her, besides the general "mary sue" vibe she gave everyb</span>
  <span id="freeText14806971462115380915" style="display:none">Okay, I have fallen hopelessly in love with Ingo since sixth grade. For some obnoxious reason, The Crossing of Ingo wasn't available in American libraries, so I had to buy it--which totally wasn't a problem because no matter how old I will get these books will always have a special place in my heart. :)<br />GOOD STUFF!:<br />To be brief, I was not disappointed!! I was SO HAPPY to see that Connor got over Elvira. I don't have any specific problem with her, besides the general "mary sue" vibe she gave everybody, but I just wasn't attached to them as a couple. Faro and Sapphire's friendship was as cute and touching as ever! :) He's so devoted to her and everyone else he loves. Even though Faro's whole "all humans are POISON!!" attitude has always ticked me off, I love him anyway. It's hard not to; even through his pride he's a good person. Sapphire has always felt like someone I would like if she were real, and that didn't change. She continued to be caring and sensitive to the world around her. As always, I loved the magical beauty that is the sea, and that is Ingo. If I had to live in a book, this would be the one. The Crossing of Ingo was a beautiful conclusion to a treasured story. I knew Sapphy would never really choose to stay in Ingo because she knew from her own personal experience from her Dad's disappearance that she couldn't cause her mother and brother (and yes, dog. Loved Sadie) that kind of pain. But it hinted at her visiting Ingo again later, so I'm not too heartbroken about her choice.<br /><br />BAD STUFF:<br />Okay, I hate it when people hurt animals like dolphins and sea turtles. I hate people destroying the ocean. People who do whaling disgust me. But SERIOUSLY. The whole "all the animals are starving" thing got real old real fast. And honestly, although I loved that the characters have grown and become more developed, and due to that, the story was also more serious because they were,I think the dying animal thing was really depressing, even for a more mature Ingo story. The Ingo books have always been very environmentally pushy, but that was because the Mer hated what many humans were doing to their home. And it was always sad when they brought that stuff up, but I understand why its needed and was always balanced and never over-pushed. Here, though, it was. <br /><br />Plus, remember how Sapphire and Connors dad basically ditched them and the woman he was married to for a sea slut? Connor got angry, but he never told his dad how he felt. For some reason Sapphy was BARELY bothered by what he did. As in, she wanted him back, but wasn't really mad. I thought this was unrealistic. Any child would probably feel angry/betrayed by getting abandoned by their father, especially if he picked some woman over them and their mother. The fact that they really weren't didn't sound like it was accurately done. Of course, they would forgive him. But they didn't feel the process that comes before that in great abundance. Plus their dad never even gave much, if any, of an apology. Lame!<br /><br />I love Faro. I really do. But Sapphire, whenever he was bashing the human race, why didn't you ever say something, ANYTHING, in our defense? Yes, most of it was true. But why didn't you mention the beach clean ups, the groups dedicated to removing dolphin-catching nets, the oil-spill clean ups, the efforts to save endangered species, the laws outlawing the hunting of whales and other creatures (I don't know about England, but whaling is illegal in the United States)? The anti-pollution laws? Why didn't she try to tell him that we recognized our mistakes and were trying to amend them as best we could? WHY?<br /><br />And this last one isn't really a complaint that matters... but even though I think Faro and Sapphy have a beautiful friendship, I was hoping that it might eventually mature into something else. Clearly, they love each other, even if it's not romantic in nature, so I thought...why not?? I hoped they would be an adorable couple since they're so meant for each other, but it didn't happen, even with all the cute "we belong to each other" stuff. So sad. But like I said, I still love them as best friends. :)<br /><br />So overall, it was a beautiful conclusion. Stormswept was pretty good too. I highly recommend the Ingo series. Mer forever!! </span>
  <a data-text-id="14806971462115380915" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_257693071" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/257693071" />
    <a title="Asavari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5577343-asavari"><img alt="Asavari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1333582770p2/5577343.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/257693071?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Asavari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Asavari" href="/user/show/5577343-asavari">Asavari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5577343-asavari?shelf=1st-person">1st-person</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5577343-asavari?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5577343-asavari?shelf=1-year-100-books-challenge-2012">1-year-100-books-challenge-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer257693071" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13638418153311928970">This review is the 6th of my 1 Year, 100 Books Challenge. For more info on this challenge and how I'll be going about it follow <a href='http://individualbutnothipster.blogspot.com.au/2012/01/1-year-100-books-challenge-about.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>this link</a><br/><br/>This <i>The Crossing of Ingo</i> was IMO the best in the Ingo series. Although I gave this book 4 stars, I won't be putting the Ingo series on my recommended shelf, but, if you are already part way through the Ingo series then make sure you read this. I was impressed by the character development in here and a good closure for the series. I wasn't sure if I was going t</span>
  <span id="freeText13638418153311928970" style="display:none">This review is the 6th of my 1 Year, 100 Books Challenge. For more info on this challenge and how I'll be going about it follow <a href="http://individualbutnothipster.blogspot.com.au/2012/01/1-year-100-books-challenge-about.html" rel="nofollow noopener">this link</a><br /><br />This <i>The Crossing of Ingo</i> was IMO the best in the Ingo series. Although I gave this book 4 stars, I won't be putting the Ingo series on my recommended shelf, but, if you are already part way through the Ingo series then make sure you read this. I was impressed by the character development in here and a good closure for the series. I wasn't sure if I was going to be reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10153731.Stormswept__Ingo___5_" title="Stormswept (Ingo, #5) by Helen Dunmore" rel="nofollow noopener">Stormswept</a> or not, but since I liked this book I probably am (also the characters sound more interesting).<br /><br /><u>The Characters:</u><br /><i>Sapphire</i> - Totally awestruck by the amount of character development that has happened to Sapphire since the first book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1022657.Ingo__Ingo___1_" title="Ingo (Ingo, #1) by Helen Dunmore" rel="nofollow noopener">Ingo</a>. She has grown from a whiny, annoying, stubborn and impulsive kid to a less annoying, less stubborn and impulsive teen. Before I got annoyed when reading about her (especially since it was her POV, so it was inescapable) but now I don't mind at all. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I'm surprised, but not unhappy, that Sapphire decided to stay on Earth, throughout the whole book it was hinted that she would stay in Ingo, with all the calling-Ingo-my-home thing. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><i>Conor</i> - the nice older brother has been my favourite character from the start of the series. He has logic!! and although logic can frequently be a sucky thing, it isn't in this series, since everyone else(besides Granny Carne, Saldowr and Roger) is like I want this, therefore it is true and I am right, so everyone should think this way so Imma go right ahead and do it, especially those with Mer blood, where as Conor thinks things through and considers consequences. I predicted that Conor wouldn't end up with Elvira because he loves his Earth lifestyle more than he loves her and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I was right, especially with the whole North thing <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I still don't see him with Rainbow though (it probably seems that way mainly because it is from Sapphire's POV and that's what she wants).<br /><br /><i>Faro and Elvira</i> - Sapphire and Conoro's Mer friends. Faro is the most annoying character in this series, he annoyed me all through the first 3 books (made worse by Sapphire taking his every word for fact) but in <i>The Crossing of Ingo</i> he was bearable. Elvira has pretty much always been a character that I have neutral feelings towards I did think her whole North craze was annoying, but it wasn't really her fault.<br /><br /><i>Other</i> - I think Ervys as a antagonist wasn't explored enough, like he has a goal and a drive (which all villains should have) but he lacks depth (which separates the good villains from the ordinary); he has no backstory, he just hates humans, hates Saldowr and wants to lead, but there is no reasons given for this, he just hates them and there was plenty of times to add a backstory in the several hundreds of pages that Ervys has been the antagonist. I liked the closure on Sapphy and Conor's dad and I felt that it was very appropriate. <br /><br /><u>The Plot:</u><br />The plot was decent and definitely an improvement on the previous book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5161.The_Deep_End_of_the_Ocean__Cappadora_Family___1_" title="The Deep End of the Ocean (Cappadora Family, #1) by Jacquelyn Mitchard" rel="nofollow noopener">The Deep</a>. But the thing I like most about the plot was the closure: the ending and the battle, it was really that which made me give it 4 stars, I liked that part more than the actual Crossing of Ingo part. I also found that part where Sapphire sees her mum in Australia totally weird but quite cool at the same time.<br /><br /><u>The Writing:</u><br />The writing style for this was decent, much like the writing in the previous books.<br /><br />This review and other reviews are also available on my blog, <a href="http://individualbutnothipster.blogspot.com.au/" rel="nofollow noopener">Individual, but not Hipster</a><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13638418153311928970" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kuhu Tri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kuhu Tri" href="/user/show/62984584-kuhu-tri">Kuhu Tri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">

                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1853057510&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1853057510" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10001050086660883824">This book was great, just like the rest of the series, but I really do think that there should be another book. In this book, Dunmore hints at the fact that maybe Sapphire's mom is part mer as well. She shows her sort of having a flashback about her experiencing the same pain that Sapphire went through when she first learned to swim with the mer. Dunmore can't just leave us hanging, and I would like to see some character development, with the mom overcoming her fear slowly and experiencing Ingo,</span>
  <span id="freeText10001050086660883824" style="display:none">This book was great, just like the rest of the series, but I really do think that there should be another book. In this book, Dunmore hints at the fact that maybe Sapphire's mom is part mer as well. She shows her sort of having a flashback about her experiencing the same pain that Sapphire went through when she first learned to swim with the mer. Dunmore can't just leave us hanging, and I would like to see some character development, with the mom overcoming her fear slowly and experiencing Ingo, and see how she reacts to it. I want to see if she becomes immersed like Sapphire, or keep her distance, like Conner</span>

<div id="review_581328917" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/581328917" />
    <a title="Maja Kron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19098217-maja-kron"><img alt="Maja Kron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484641864p2/19098217.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/581328917?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja Kron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja Kron" href="/user/show/19098217-maja-kron">Maja Kron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer581328917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12444014486258902724">Even though I read the first 3 books in this series when I was younger it wasn't until quite recently I found out that this book exists and I've been so excitd to read it since then, and I'm so happy I have because I loved every single moment of this. <br/><br/>I loved being back in the world of Ingo and to follow all the characters once again on a new journey. Another thing I really like about these books is that they're so much about the ocean (yes I know it's a mermaid book so that's kind of the point)</span>
  <span id="freeText12444014486258902724" style="display:none">Even though I read the first 3 books in this series when I was younger it wasn't until quite recently I found out that this book exists and I've been so excitd to read it since then, and I'm so happy I have because I loved every single moment of this. <br /><br />I loved being back in the world of Ingo and to follow all the characters once again on a new journey. Another thing I really like about these books is that they're so much about the ocean (yes I know it's a mermaid book so that's kind of the point), but what I mean is that they're so aware of it. They're bringing up real life issues like pollution of the water, the killing of whales and dolphins caught in nets, and that's not something many other mermaid books do. These books are truly takes you on a journey through the oceans and teach you a lot about it, and that's partly why this is my favorite mermaid series. <br /><br />I didn't expect it to have such a bittersweet ending, it was sad but beautiful at the same time, and this was a perfect way to wrap this series up. Even though this is more of a middle grade series I'll read and love this for the rest of my life, and I will recommend it to anyone who's looking for a book about the ocean or mermaids! <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12444014486258902724" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1687489915" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1687489915" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51465228-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553415474p2/51465228.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1687489915?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/51465228-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1687489915" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1013540937557424306">I'm so glad Dunmore decided to write this fourth book of the 'Ingo' series, even though originally the series was to only be a trilogy. Dunmore continues to create the believable underwater world of Ingo with her fabulous, often lyrical, descriptions.<br/><br/>For me "The crossing of Ingo" is the most action packed book in the series as Sapphire, Conor, Elvira and Faro answer the call to cross Ingo - a long and dangerous journey that only the strongest young Mer can make. With Ervys and his followers dete</span>
  <span id="freeText1013540937557424306" style="display:none">I'm so glad Dunmore decided to write this fourth book of the 'Ingo' series, even though originally the series was to only be a trilogy. Dunmore continues to create the believable underwater world of Ingo with her fabulous, often lyrical, descriptions.<br /><br />For me "The crossing of Ingo" is the most action packed book in the series as Sapphire, Conor, Elvira and Faro answer the call to cross Ingo - a long and dangerous journey that only the strongest young Mer can make. With Ervys and his followers determined to stop the human children from completing the crossing - dead or alive - the four friends begin their journey. At times things appear too easy for them considering how perilous the crossing is supposed to be. However, the book reaches a great climax and comes to a satisfying conclusion, although not all the loose ends are brought together. A worthy finish to a great series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1013540937557424306" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5727270036050086766">I really enjoyed the first 3 books in the Ingo series, and this one was no exception. It kept me in the world of Ingo, and I stayed up till about 2 am to finish it. Probably not smart when I had to get up at 6 the next day (or that day, since it was after 12.) I digress.<br/><br/>This book was spent mostly in Ingo, unlike the other books where it was back and forth. And I enjoyed that. It made the world of Ingo more alive to me, to know what it was like more, becuase Sapphy was getting to understand it be</span>
  <span id="freeText5727270036050086766" style="display:none">I really enjoyed the first 3 books in the Ingo series, and this one was no exception. It kept me in the world of Ingo, and I stayed up till about 2 am to finish it. Probably not smart when I had to get up at 6 the next day (or that day, since it was after 12.) I digress.<br /><br />This book was spent mostly in Ingo, unlike the other books where it was back and forth. And I enjoyed that. It made the world of Ingo more alive to me, to know what it was like more, becuase Sapphy was getting to understand it better, too. <br /><br />It had a bittersweet ending, which I thought was according, it was the end of a series, that makes it sad automatically, but there was death, but there was also life, and love. <br /><br />All in all, a good book, and I hope you check out the series, it's really good. <br /></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/880388736?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/5861493-michelle">Michelle</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007270262" href="/book/show/3839707-the-crossing-of-ingo">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5861493-michelle?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer880388736" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2260863995631270708">This is the 4th book in the Ingo series. Conor and Sapphire have been called to take the rite of passage of the Mer, the Crossing of Ingo, which is a journey around the underwater world of Ingo. Their inclusion angers Erys and his faction that want to keep the Mer pure, but they are able to take the journey along with their friends Faro and Elvira. Along the way, they are harried by the sharks who have allied themselves with Erys, but are befriended by the dolphins. They take the unconventional </span>
  <span id="freeText2260863995631270708" style="display:none">This is the 4th book in the Ingo series. Conor and Sapphire have been called to take the rite of passage of the Mer, the Crossing of Ingo, which is a journey around the underwater world of Ingo. Their inclusion angers Erys and his faction that want to keep the Mer pure, but they are able to take the journey along with their friends Faro and Elvira. Along the way, they are harried by the sharks who have allied themselves with Erys, but are befriended by the dolphins. They take the unconventional path of circumnavigating from the north to avoid the traps Erys has set. Each has trials and challenges along the way, knowing that if they succeed, they must face Erys when they return in a final showdown. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2260863995631270708" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jmd4RxFjIhfwwuPQFSzD7FqTobkg2fYOzD6Wn1xu2FbHYAsDPDdS56hHDviMUtm4jRe/vqYNrJcHmm/G98t/uw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HQHTq4iu2PcXzAbMuXLRc/q7x8joxJHdQ97qFMRoTNBUBqDvpfqoB09J6+QgDMsnLT/Zz24Qy0SIehNNb83rPQ==')})
  }
//]]>

Jim Stanford\'s book is an anti<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText17705041574493623722\" style=\"display:none\">Economics is too important to be left to economists. This brilliantly concise and readable book provides non-specialist readers with all the information they need to understand how capitalism works (and how it doesn\'t). Jim Stanford\'s book is an antidote to the abstract and ideological way that economics is normally taught and reported. Key concepts such as finance, competition and wage labor are explored, and their importance to everyday life is revealed. Stanford answers questions such as &quot;Do workers need capitalists?&quot;, &quot;Why does capitalism harm the environment?&quot;, and &quot;What really happens on the stock market?&quot; He offers both a realistic assessment of capitalism\'s strengths, and a robust critique of its many failures. This book will appeal to those working for a fairer world, and students of social sciences who need to engage with economics. p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.37 avg rating &mdash; 3,105 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1997\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer10109030231002369052\">This is a no-holds-barred response to the liberal and conservative retreat from an assertive, activist, and socially transformative civil rights agenda of recent years--using a black feminist lens and the issue of  the impact of recent legislation, s<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText10109030231002369052\" style=\"display:none\">This is a no-holds-barred response to the liberal and conservative retreat from an assertive, activist, and socially transformative civil rights agenda of recent years--using a black feminist lens and the issue of  the impact of recent legislation, social policy, and welfare &quot;reform&quot; on black women\'s--especially poor black women\'s--control over their bodies\' autonomy and their freedom to bear and raise children with respect and dignity in a society whose white mainstream is determined to demonize, even criminalize their lives.   It gives its readers a cogent legal and historical argument for a radically new , and socially transformative, definition of  &quot;liberty&quot; and &quot;equality&quot; for the American polity from a black feminist perspective.The author is able to combine the most innovative and radical thinking on several fronts--racial theory, feminist, and legal--to produce a work that is at once history and political treatise.  By using the history of how American law--beginning with slavery--has treated the issue of the state\'s right  to interfere with the black woman\'s body, the author explosively and effectively makes the case for the legal redress to the racist implications of current policy with regards to 1) access to and coercive dispensing of birth control to poor black women 2) the criminalization of parenting by poor black women who have used drugs 3) the stigmatization and devaluation of poor black mothers under the new welfare provisions, and 4) the differential access to and disproportionate spending of social resources on the new reproductive technologies used by wealthy white couples to insure genetically related offspring.The legal redress of the racism inherent in current  American law and policy in these matters, the author argues in her last chapter, demands and should lead us to adopt a new standard and definition of the liberal theory of &quot;liberty&quot; and &quot;equality&quot; based on the need for, and the positive role of government in fostering, social as well as individual justice.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"10109030231002369052\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/41542.Helen_Dunmore">About Helen Dunmore</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/41542.Helen_Dunmore"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1292177072p3/41542.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/41542.Helen_Dunmore">Helen Dunmore
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
812
followers
</div>

</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15142208870269814896">I was born in December 1952, in Yorkshire, the second of four children. My father was the eldest of twelve, and this extended family has no doubt had a strong influence on my life, as have my own children. In a large family you hear a great many stories. You also come to understand very early that stories hold quite different meanings for different listeners, and can be recast from many viewpoints</span>
  <span id="freeText15142208870269814896" style="display:none">I was born in December 1952, in Yorkshire, the second of four children. My father was the eldest of twelve, and this extended family has no doubt had a strong influence on my life, as have my own children. In a large family you hear a great many stories. You also come to understand very early that stories hold quite different meanings for different listeners, and can be recast from many viewpoints.<br /><br />Poetry was very important to me from childhood. I began by listening to and learning by heart all kinds of rhymes and hymns and ballads, and then went on to make up my own poems, using the forms I’d heard. Writing these down came a little later.<br /><br />I studied English at the University of York, and after graduation taught English as a foreign language in Finland.<br /><br />At around this time I began to write the poems which formed my first poetry collection, The Apple Fall, and to publish these in magazines. I also completed two novels; fortunately neither survives, and it was more than ten years before I wrote another novel.<br /><br />During this time I published several collections of poems, and wrote some of the short stories which were later collected in Love of Fat Men. I began to travel a great deal within the UK and around the world, for poetry tours and writing residences. This experience of working in many different countries and cultures has been very important to my work. I reviewed poetry for Stand and Poetry Review and later for The Observer, and subsequently reviewed fiction for The Observer, The Times and The Guardian. My critical work includes introductions to the poems of Emily Brontë, the short stories of D H Lawrence and F Scott Fitzgerald, a study of Virginia Woolf’s relationships with women and Introductions to the Folio Society's edition of Anna Karenina and to the new Penguin Classics edition of Tolstoy's My Confession. <br /><br />During the 1980s and early 1990s I taught poetry and creative writing, tutored residential writing courses for the Arvon Foundation and took part in the Poetry Society's Writer in Schools scheme, as well as giving readings and workshops in schools, hospitals, prisons and every other kind of place where a poem could conceivably be welcome. I also taught at the University of Glamorgan, the University of Bristol's Continuing Education Department and for the Open College of the Arts.<br /><br />In the late 1980s I began to publish short stories, and these were the beginning of a breakthrough into fiction. What I had learned of prose technique through the short story gave me the impetus to start writing novels. My first novel for children was Going to Egypt, published in 1992, and my first novel for adults was Zennor in Darkness, published in 1993, which won the McKitterick Prize. This was also my first researched novel, set in the First World War and dealing with the period when D H Lawrence and his wife Frieda lived in Zennor in Cornwall, and came under suspicion as German spies.<br /><br />My third novel, A Spell of Winter, won the inaugural Orange Prize for Fiction in 1996, and since then I have published a number of novels, short story collections and books for children. Full details of all these books are available on this website. The last of The Ingo Quartet, The Crossing of Ingo, was published in paperback in Spring 2009.<br /><br />My seventh novel, The Siege (2001) was shortlisted both for the Whitbread Novel Award and the Orange Prize for Fiction. This was another researched novel, which grew from a lifelong love of Russian history, culture and literature. It is is set in Leningrad during the first year of the siege of the city by German forces, which lasted for 880 days from the fall of Mga on 30th August 1941. The Siege has been translated into Russian by Tatyana Averchina, and extracts have been broadcast on radio in St Petersburg. House of Orphans was published in 2006, and in 2008 Counting the Stars. Its central characters are the Roman poet Catullus, who lived during the last years of the Republic, </span>
  <a data-text-id="15142208870269814896" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
